11.4        Modifications in RAP
Any project must be based on the rational choice of the people,
especially those who might be adversely affected by it. Only such an
approach ensure both that displacement is minimised and that the
-project really serves the public purpose.
The right to decide whether any process of project has a public
purpose or in the national interest may rest with the people who will be
affected by it both displaced persons and those who might
accommodate them -subsequently. Peoples' participation in the
formulating and selection of a project also ensures that those who are
going to be PAPs are not made victims but rather partners in the
-  _                      development.
The PIC conducted through participatory approach has lead to
following major modifications in the RAP.
Free toll for project land owners: All the PAPs whose land is
acquired should be permitted to free use of highway. This may be
regulated by allowing only one commercial and one non-
commercial vehicle per affected family. After due verification of the
PAPs, the project can issue a letter to PAP to use highway without
paying toll.
-  Private lands and houses which gets isolated or cut off due to
acquisition of land in the project, may also be acquired if the
owner gives his/her consent to such acquisition. This would apply
only to oustees who can not make economic or any other use of
Kirloskar Consultants Limited
11.12



EnvironmenitalandSocialAssesment Report      cnlpr-T7
-advdaVa-HaJol Road                           Public lnformaton and Consutation
- Flnatisaton of R&R Action Plan
their non-acquired assets. Furfural Chemicals Pvt. Ltd. is one
such case where at Baska bypass the road divides the defunct
factory premises in to two disjoint parts of which the company can
not make economic use and hence option to completely purchase
the factory premises of the said company is worked out. Similarly,
Mr. Ashwin Sheth and his family members own 65 Ha. of land in
Asoj village and bypass at Asoj generates a triangular section of
land between existing road and the proposed bypass. This
triangular section of land can not be utilised further for economic
purpose by the owner and hence should be purchased by the
project. During the execution of the project such options will have
to be worked out by making PAPs participate in the discussion.
Changes in the curve Alignment: During PIC, all alternative
leading to non-displacement were studied. Different alternatives
on the basis of technical and social merits and demerits of the
project were examined and made available to public. It has lead to
many changes in RAP. Firstly, land at the curve alignment in the
Asoj bypass belonging to Mr. Ashwin Sheth has been improved in
order to minimise the loss in the utility of his land after land
acquisition. At many places, minor curve improvement or
reduction in ROW  subject to technical feasibility and social
acceptability are made. Secondly, in three project villages need for
access to the other side of the road was strongly demanded by
the villagers which led to provision of underpasses in the final
design. This has also enhanced safety levels of the villagers and
animals crossing the road.
11.5        Concluding Remarks
The PIC process has resulted in acceptance of the proposed
alignment, identification of community concem at large and possible
acceptable solutions, both at individual level and community level.
These will be generalised approximately while formulating the RAP.
It needs to be mentioned here that discussions with each PAP should
be done as a follow-up by the NGO, exploring the available solutions
suiting the individual considering his/her socio-economic background
so as to ensure adherence to the IL & FS R&R policy.

Vadodara-Halol Road                                       Resettlement Action Plan
- Provisions for Implementation
12.1.        Objectives
The basic objective of the Resettlement Action Plan (RAP) is to ensure
that the PAPs from the 'corridor of impact' of VHRP get adequate
compensation and assistance so as to achieve or improve their pre-
:project economical status in the shortest time and retain their potential
for further economic growth.
12.2.        Key Steps
The key steps in developing the RAP are:
.1  Development of an entitlement package that provides details of
compensation and renabilitation assistance;
2. Integration of RAP implementation with the project execution:
3. Provision of instituticnal set up and budget for implementation of
the RAP; and
4. Provision for arrangement for monitoring the implementation of the
RAP.
The following sections present details on each of the above aspect with
respect to acquisition of the lands for the VHRP.
12.3         Entitlement Package
12.3.1       Loss of Land
Considering the project design and its deviations from the existing
ROW, the VHRP covering 31.5 Km of road improvement will require
acquisition of estimated 79.16 Ha of land in Vadodara district and 28.77
Ha in Panchamahal districts (total 107.93 Ha) from the private land
owners. The details of the extent of land to be acquired and the number
of land holders losing land are given in Table - 8.9 and Annexures IA,
IB and ll.
Land Owner PAFs
For developing the entitlement for the land owner PAFs, the socio-
economic data was analyze&Tor individual families and details on the
following parameters were extracted:
-  family size and number of adult members in the family:
* agricultural, non-agncultural and total income;
* loss of land to project, compensation for land' and balance land
holding after LA;
- post-LA income with and without interest earnings accruing from
compensation and gain/loss with respect to pre-LA income, and
Compensation is estimated based on market salue of land derived through local enquirics, 30%
; .J.................. solatium and 12% intcrest, it is Rs. 503,484/Ha and Rs. 251,742/Ha for irrigated and unirrigated land
rcspectively.
Kirloskar Consultants Limited
12-1



Enwirnmental and Sdial Assessment Report                       Cliapter-12
J--doda,a.HaIol Road                                  Resetfement Action Plan
-Pmvisions for implementatIon
*  vulnerable families/members in a family such as widows, aged
persons and woman headed family.
With the reported cropping pattem and general yield. while analysing
the data on income, it was observed that some families reported
income which prima facie appeared to be lower than that which could
have been obtained from their land holdings. Therefore the size of the
land holding and absence of non-agricultural income were considered
as the main parameters for categorizing the PAPs into category 1, 2
and 3 corresponding to marginally, moderately and severely affected
groups as defined in section 10.2.3. Out of the 50 families surveyed,
complete information for developing the entitlement package was
analysed for only 50 families. The results of such analysis are
presented in Annexure Ill.
In case there are standing agricultural crops at the time of LA, cash
compensation equivalent to one year income for crops will be paid
through contingency fund. In case of loss of fruit bearing trees, the
income compensation will be for made for a period of 12 years.
Land Tenants
In the absence of information about the profile of land tenants, as
discussed in section 10.3, the entitlement for tenants is based on the
estimated land under tenancy from the plot numbers identified. The
total land under tenancy is estimated as 25.45 ha (16.72 ha. - irrigated
and 7.73 ha.- unirrigated). The pattern of land plot sizes is assumed to
be similar to the land holdings under LA from private owners. Since only
severely affected tenants are to be provided land equal to MEL, it is
assumed that such requirements will be limited to 10 tenants and the
remaining will be assisted through loans / grants.
Industnal Land
Only one case of industrial land loss of a defunct factory exists. The
land value was estimated through inquiries with Gujarat Industrial
Development Board (being industrial land) as Rs. 170,000/Acre i.e.
Rs.419,900/ha. The compensation will be based on this figure.
Loss of Village Land
The public land acquired within the revenue boundary of the village can
belong to either the Gram Panchayat or the Revenue Department,
GoG. In case of the government land, since the GoG is a member
(shareholder) of SPV, and since the project (road) will be transferred
back to the govemment, no compensation is proposed to be paid for
such government lands.' As the gram panchayat / govemment land
holding is yet to be identified through JMS, it is proposed to pay a price
to the Gram Panchayat for such lands at the govemment rate from the
contingency provision.
12.3.2      Loss of Structures
Residential Houses
Ten houses are to be demolished for the proposed road improvement.
Seven of these houses are occupied by the owners themselves, 2
Kirloskar consultants Limited
12-2



-J : i. ; 01 X \Envronmental and Social Assessment Repor.                             Chaptor-12
Vadodara-HaJl Road                                     Resettement Action Plan
_  Provisions for Implementation
houses have been rented to tenants and 1 house is owned by a
squatter.
As per IL&FS policies, all house owners are compensated by a house
of area equal to the area of the lost structure. In case the area of the
house is less than the minimum government norm for single family
dwelling, a house of minimum area is provided (Indira Awas Vikas
Yojana). For squatters, irrespective of the size for the present dwelling,
an ownership house of minimum area as per government norm is
provided. The beneficiary under this case however cannot sell the
house till completion of the concession period of the project.
In the case of VHRP all residential structures are below 32.5 sq.m. (350
sq.ft.) in area and therefore all entitlement are restricted to houses with
built-up area of 32.5 sq.m. and surrounding open area of equal
dimension. The cost including the cost of land for such houses at the
rate of Rs. 1075/sq.m. (Rs. 100/sq.ft.) is estimated to be Rs. 40,000.
In the case of tenants, it is expected that they will re-establish
themselves elsewhere and the IL&FS policy entitles them only for a
shifting allowance. However in the present cases, the tenants belong to
economically weaker sections and are living in damaged houses due to
financial constraints. It is difficult to envisage that they will be able to
shift -to altemate accommodation and re-establish themselves. As a
special case, therefore, these tenants will also be provided with a
dwelling unit of minimum area. The house owner will be compensated
for the land and structure based on valuation.
A shiffing allowance of Rs. 1000 will be provided to each of the 10
PAPs.
Commercial Structures
As identified in Annexure V, the only commercial structures requiring
relocation are movable stalls. Hence a shifting allowance at the rate of
Rs. 1000 per structure is proposed for them.
Fencin
Compensation for rebuilding barbed fencing or compound walls will be
given to the PAPs listed in Annexure V.
Industrial Structure
Considering that the factory at Baska is defunct. its valuation will be
'done to determine the cost of compensation for the structures. This will
be paid through contingency funds.
Other Public Structures
Compensation for rebuilding/relocating other public structures such as
temples, bus stop and wells will be provided.

Table - 12.1 summarizes the proposed entitlement package norms for
making  necessary  budgetary  provisions  based   on   above
considerations.

12.6        Institutional Arrangement For Implementing The RAP
12.6.1       Implementation Responsibility
It is primarily the responsibility of the SPV to ensure successful
implementation of the project. The construction of the project mainly
involves acquisition of private agricultural land to the extent of more
than 85% of the total requirement. The entitlement package developed
for individual PAFs indicate that about 20% families will require a
grantloan/altemate land for restoration of their pre-project status.
Adequate  institutional  arrangements  for  cperationalizing  the
mechanism for assistance is necessary for successful implementation
of RAP. Therefore there is a need to focus on two main issues:
*  Issues related to LA and altemate land allocation for severely
7dlYeC;d PRAfs and..
*  Issues related to Economic Rehabilitation (ER) of PAFs.
Land acquisition is primarily the govemment responsibility and a
mutually acceptable compensation at market rate is to be arrived at
through negotiations. The SPV is committed to pay the difference
between the compensation amount as per govemment rates and the
negotiated settlement price of the land. The procedure therefore will
involve interaction and consensus building with the PAFs on an
agreeable fair rate of compensation.
Economic Rehabilitation of PAFs is necessary so that their pre-project
income levels are enhanced or at least retained. It is essential that the
compensation paid to the PAFs is utilized to build assets for
Kirloskar consultants Limited
12-10



EnvironmentalandSocialAssessment Report                          Chapter-12
Vadodarar--aol Road                                     Resettement Actfon Plin
Provisions for Implementation
substituting the loss of income to the PAFs. Since grants and loans
are proposed to be given to the severely affected PAFs as means to
raise the income levels, in addition to compensation for land (cash or
land equal to MEL), it is necessary to identify local business activities
or provide vocational training to utilize these gra^ts/loans to build
assets.
In this context, it is necessary that a NGO exoerienced in LA
procedures and in implementing income generatic: schemes work
closely with  SPV  and  govemment. Thus the implementation
responsibility through an institutional arrangemen- will need to be
developed around the SPV, GoG Representative and NGO
involvement.
12.6.2      Land Acquisition
LA for the project is the responsibility of the Revenue Department
which is done through a Special Deputy Collectc" or District Land
Acquisition Officer (LAO) at the district level. The LA programme will
be implemented in two districts viz., Vadodara ard Panchamahals
simultaneously. Therefore, there will be two LAOs, one for each
district to manage all LA activities for the project. Land plan schedules
indicating the details of the lands required have been prepared by the
Executive Engineer and submitted to the Distnct LAO who has
initiated LA proceedings uls 4(i) in October 1996. Separate
institutional arrangement, other than the existing one is not envisaged
for this purpose.
In addition, there is also is a need to allocate compensatory land to
the severely affected PAPs. There are two options: (1) finding out
govemment land for allotment to PAPs and (2) extending cash
assistance to help the people to purchase land in the open market.
The field observations indicate that govemment lands are of inferior
quality and most of it is already in occupation by the local farmers for
cultivation. The land holders losing land for VHRP have expressed
their reluctance to accept these lands. Therefore. the possibilities of
finding altemate govemment land is extremely limited. The only
alternative therefore is to help the PAPs to find suitable - lands in the
open market.
Thus a district-wise Compensatory Land Procurement Committee
(Annexure VI) for each of the two districts is prcoosed to facilitate
identification, purchase and transfer/allocation of land to the severely
affected PAPs. The committee will help the PAPs identify sellers of
land, assess the extent and the market value of land available. The
committee will thus bring the seller of the land and the PAPs together
and help them  negotiate the price of the land and settle the
transaction. The NGO will ensure that the interests of the PAPs is
addressed - both in land acquisition as well as compensatory land
allocation. The committee will also decide the rate of compensation
from private lands and mechanisms for its disbsrsement for each
PAF.

12.6.3      Economic Rehabilitation
This is one of the critical areas of project implementation. It is
proposed to set up two committees as under:
x Project Level R&R Monitoring Committee (Annexure Vil): The
main function of this committee will be to ensure that the
proposed ER measures are being implemented as planned. make
policy decisions to facilitate implementation of the same and give
necessary administrative decisions/directions as required.
*  District Level R&R Implementing Committee (Annexure Vill).
The main function of this committee is to implement the identified
ER program.
12.7        Role Of NGO
12.7.1      Responsibilities
In the present context, an NGO will work as a link between the project
(more specifically the SPV) and the affected community. It will
educate PAPs on the need to implement the project, on aspects
relating to LA and ER measures and ensure proper utilisation of
various grants and loans being extended to them under the R&R
entitlement package. Specifically, the selected NGOs will be
responsible for:
i) identification and profiling of land PAPs who could not be
contacted in this study in both the districts and develop rapport
with adversely affected PAPs, the project authorities and district
LAOs;
ii) exploring the possibilities of negotiated settlements for the lands
acquired for the project and help PAPs negotiate properly with the
project authorities and the LAO;
iii) identification of vulnerable sections losing their land who could not
be covered in this study;
iv) verification of the land records of the affected PAPs at the time of
-                       :  project implementation to-be carried out to establish the total land
owned by each individual and the extent of loss (follow-up by
NGO);
v) detailing of land owners having land holdings less than MEL
holding and assisting themn during the LA to enhance their holding
to MEL level by providing adjacent lands or to sell their lands to
the project and obtain alternate land;
vi) verification of land tenants and their eligibility for ER based on the
cutoff date (date of notification uls 4(1) in October 1996;
vii) working out entitlement (RAP on individual basis);.
viii).assisting in speedy implementation of ER measures such as
provision of land (if it takes more than six months) by taking up
Kirloskar Consultants Limited

the issue with Project Level ER Implementation Committee for
appropriate measures;
ix) assisting severely affected (and other eligible PAPs) in obtaining
vocational training from various govemment development and
other suitable training programmes for income generation
schemes;
x) ensuring proper utilisation of various grants as available under ER
package;
xi) help PAPs in the redressal of their grievances relating to LA and
ER; and
xii) any other responsibilities as may be assigned by the project
authorities for the welfare of the affected community.
12.7.2      Selection Of NGO
It is of utmost important to select an NGO which is good, genuine and
committed to the task assigned. NGO having local presence and
experience to deal with land acquisition issues and social problems
like resettlement will be preferred. Since the magnitude of R&R is
relatively small, only one NGO will be selected for the project to help
the District Level ER Implementation Committee in the implementation
of the RAP. Selection of NGO will be done by SPV for a period of
three years.
12.7.3      Contracting NGOs
NGO will be involved in the implementation of the RAP through
mutually agreed upon terms and conditions with specific
responsibilities and adequate in-built accountability. A Memorandum
of Understanding (MoU) will be signed with the selected NGO
indicating the tasks to be performed and the amount to be paid for
their services. The payment to the NGO will be linked to the
performance of the task assigned and the time period. The payment
will be arranged on quarterly basis to be released on certification of
completing the previous task. The NGO will periodically submit a
progress report before claiming its next installment of the contracted
amount. Its services will be required for three years. The draft terms
-                     of reference for NGO is detailed in Annexure-IX.
12.8       . Role Of Other Government Agencies
Various govemment departments and public agencies particularly the
Revenue, Rural Development (RD) and Bank/Financial Institutions
have an important to make in implementing the RAP. The Revenue
Department is responsible not only for acquiring the land and other
properties and handing them over to the project authorities but it is
also required to allot available government land for housing and
agricultural purposes. The District Rural Development Agency can
extend the income generation schemes and skills development
programmes for the welfare of the community, especially the severely
affected PAPs to integrate various development schemes for their ER.
It should be noted that the funding for the participation in the

12.9        Implementation Schedule
The implementation schedule depends largely on the decision of
contracting the project in two or more stretches. The schedule
proposed below assumes that it will be taken up in two stretches
simultaneously. Land should be taken into possession and handed
over to project authorities (preferably free from all encumbrances) for
carrying out constructional activities.
The first activity of the project, as far as LA is concemed is the issue
of a notification u/s 4(1) of the LA Act, 1894 as amended in 1984 LA
takes minimum of 9 months to complete and it was initiated in October
-- 1996. However, its further follow-up al described in chapter 9 is yet to
commence. Compensation needs to be paid to the PAPs before the
start of actual project construction. In case of any delay in LA
proceedings, R&B will take lands from their owners on 'consent basis'.
The implementation schedule is reflected in the annual phasing of
budget funds wherein it is assumed that 75% land acquisition and
related ER will be done in the first year itself, while the balance will be
done in the second year. Implementation schedule of 2 years has
been worked out on the general LA proceedings. Delays if any in the
LA cannot be specifically addressed. However, to accelerate the
process of acquiring land, negotiated settlement can be given top
priority.
The activities to be taken on an immediate basis as a part of initiating
the implementation of the RAP are as follows:
i3    Issue of notification u/s 4(1) of the LA Act for acquiring private
properties - done in October 1996;
ii)    Selection and appointment of NGOs;
iii)   Conduction of survey of all the land owners and tenants to
identify the PAPs and their entitlement requirements;
iv)    Constituting land operationalising the following:
a)    Project Level -ER Monitoring Committee
District Level ER Implementation Committee
c)    Compensation Land Procurement Committee
iv)   Payment of compensation as per LA Act or as per amount
agreed through negotiated settlement. This is the responsibility
of LAO and SPV.
v)    Allocation of govemment land and release of grants to the
PAPs for purchase of either land or productive assets. DRO
and NGO will work jointly to ensure that grants reach genuine
persons.
Subsequent to the above mentioned, focus will be on the follow-up
actions particularly on promoting economic activities and their

12.10       Monitoring And Evaluation
The M&E will be done simultaneous with the implementation of the LA
& RAP. For this purpose, while conventional government monitoring,
as described in subsequent sections will continue which mostly relates
to LA and compensation, number of families displaced and resettled,
extent of government land identified and allotted to the PAPs, other
R&R assistance extended and the related financial aspects etc., An
extemal agency will be engaged to meaningfully and realistically
evaluate R&R programmes on periodic basis. Further arrangements
for M&E are discussed below:
Project Level Monitoring
The SPV will be responsible for setting up and putting in place a
monitoring framework for the R&R implementation of the RAP. Since
M&E will be simultaneous with the initiation of R&R activities, the SPV
will beforehand develop a prescribed proforma for monitoring at
different levels - project and district. Such a monitoring system will
help in developing quality control and planning for remedial measures
to overcome implementation problems and build them into the
programme of activities. Besides various physical and financial
aspects, preparation of quarterly progress reports on the progress of
R&R activities will form the important task of the SPV.
In order to strengthen monitoring of LA & ER programmes, Project
Level Monitoring Committee (Annexure VII) will be constituted. The
committee will meet once in three months to approve plans and
monitor implementation of R&R activities. It will advise the project staff
at the district level through the District Level Committees on various
aspects of the programmes to make implementation more effective.
Monitoring by IL&FS
IL&FS will monitor social aspects of-the project on an on-going basis
through a Social Audit. The Environmental and Social Management
Group (ESMG) which comprises specialists with adequate expertise
and skill to understand the critical issues concerning environmental
and social aspects will undertake it.
District Level Monitoring
Concurrent monitoring at the district level will be the responsibility of
the District Level ER Implementation Committees (Annexure Vil) and
Compensatory Land Acquisition Committee (Annexure VI). They will
provide a feed back on the progress of LA and ER programmes to the
Project Level Monitoring Committee in prescribed monitoring formats.
12.11       Evaluation Of ER Programmes
An independent agency not associated with the project execution will
be engaged to carry out the impact evaluation of the implementation



Vadodara-Haloi Road                                     Resettement Action Plan
Provisions for lmplwnentation
of R&R programmes. Impact evaluation on sample basis need to be
undertaken twice during the project period. The first evaluation can
take place half way through the project and final evaluation at the
completion of implementing the RAP. The mid term evaluation will
help to plan for corrective measures while the final evaluation will
provide base for changes in the approach and policy to deal with the
problems relating to involuntary resettlement arising out of road
project. Provisions have been made in the budget for engaging the
external agency for impact evaluation.
